Once any of the rules are met,\n   266→\t// the \"SucceededCriteriaMet\" condition is added, and the lingering pods are removed.\n   267→\t// The terminal state for such a Job has the \"Complete\" condition.\n   268→\t// Additionally, these rules are evaluated in order; Once the Job meets one of the rules,\n   269→\t// other rules are ignored. If this field is set to zero,\n   416→\t// the Job becomes eligible to be deleted immediately after it finishes.\n   417→\t// +optional\n   418→\tTTLSecondsAfterFinished *int32\n   419→\n   420→\t// completionMode specifies how Pod completions are tracked. Each Pod completion is\n   425→\t// homologous to each other.\n   426→\t//\n   427→\t// `Indexed` means that the Pods of a\n   428→\t// Job get an associated completion index from 0 to (.spec.completions - 1),\n   429→\t// available in the annotation batch.kubernetes.io/job-completion-index.\n   430→\t// The Job is considered complete when there is one successfully completed Pod\n   431→\t// for each index.\n   432→\t// When value is `Indexed`, .spec.completions must be specified and\n   433→\t// `.spec.parallelism` must be less than or equal to 10^5.\n   434→\t// In addition, The Pod name takes the form\n   435→\t// `$(job-name)-$(index)-$(random-string)`,\n   436→\t// the Pod hostname takes the form `$(job-name)-$(index)`.\n   437→\t//\n   438→\t// More completion modes can be added in the future.\n   439→\t// If the Job controller observes a mode that it doesn't recognize, which\n   440→\t// is possible during upgrades due to version skew, the controller\n   441→\t// skips updates for the Job.\n   442→\t// +optional\n   443→\tCompletionMode *CompletionMode\n   444→\n   445→\t// suspend specifies whether the Job controller should create Pods or not. If\n   446→\t// a Job is created with suspend set to true, no Pods are created by the Job\n   447→\t// controller. If a Job is suspended after creation (i.e. the flag goes from\n   448→\t// false to true), the Job controller will delete all active Pods associated\n   449→\t// with this Job. Users must design their workload to gracefully handle this.\n   450→\t// Suspending a Job will reset the StartTime field of the Job, effectively\n   451→\t// resetting the ActiveDeadlineSeconds timer too. Defaults to false.\n   452→\t//\n   453→\t// +optional\n   454→\tSuspend *bool\n   455→\n   456→\t// podReplacementPolicy specifies when to create replacement Pods.\n   457→\t// Possible values are:\n   458→\t// - TerminatingOrFailed means that we recreate pods\n   459→\t//   when they are terminating (has a metadata.deletionTimestamp) or failed.\n   460→\t// - Failed means to wait until a previously created Pod is fully terminated (has phase\n   461→\t//   Failed or Succeeded) before creating a replacement Pod.\n   462→\t//\n   463→\t// When using podFailurePolicy, Failed is the the only allowed value.\n   464→\t// TerminatingOrFailed and Failed are allowed values when podFailurePolicy is not in use.\n   465→\t// This is an beta field. To use this, enable the JobPodReplacementPolicy feature toggle.\n   466→\t// This is on by default.\n   467→\t// +optional\n   468→\tPodReplacementPolicy *PodReplacementPolicy\n   469→\n   470→\t// ManagedBy field indicates the controller that manages a Job. The k8s Job\n   471→\t// controller reconciles jobs which don't have this field at all or the field\n   472→\t// value is the reserved string `kubernetes.io/job-controller`, but skips\n   473→\t// reconciling Jobs with a custom value for this field.\n   474→\t// The value must be a valid domain-prefixed path (e.g. acme.io/foo) -\n   475→\t// all characters before the first \"/\" must be a valid subdomain as defined\n   476→\t// by RFC 1123. All characters trailing the first \"/\" must be valid HTTP Path\n   477→\t// characters as defined by RFC 3986. The value cannot exceed 63 characters.\n   478→\t// This field is immutable.\n   479→\t//\n   480→\t// This field is beta-level. The job controller accepts setting the field\n   481→\t// when the feature gate JobManagedBy is enabled (enabled by default).\n   482→\t// +optional\n   483→\tManagedBy *string\n   484→}\n   485→\n   486→// JobStatus represents the current state of a Job.\n   487→type JobStatus struct {\n   488→\n   489→\t// The latest available observations of an object's current state. When a Job\n   490→\t// fails, one of the conditions will have type \"Failed\" and status true. When\n   491→\t// a Job is suspended, one of the conditions will have type \"Suspended\" and\n   492→\t// status true; when the Job is resumed, the status of this condition will\n   493→\t// become false. When a Job is completed, one of the conditions will have\n   494→\t// type \"Complete\" and status true.\n   495→\t//\n   496→\t// A job is considered finished when it is in a terminal condition, either\n   497→\t// \"Complete\" or \"Failed\". A Job cannot have both the \"Complete\" and \"Failed\" conditions.\n   498→\t// Additionally, it cannot be in the \"Complete\" and \"FailureTarget\" conditions.\n   499→\t// The \"Complete\", \"Failed\" and \"FailureTarget\" conditions cannot be disabled.\n   500→\t//\n   501→\t// +optional\n   502→\tConditions []JobCondition\n   503→\n   504→\t// Represents time when the job controller started processing a job. When a\n   505→\t// Job is created in the suspended state, this field is not set until the\n   506→\t// first time it is resumed. This field is reset every time a Job is resumed\n   507→\t// from suspension. It is represented in RFC3339 form and is in UTC.\n   508→\t//\n   509→\t// Once set, the field can only be removed when the job is suspended.\n   510→\t// The field cannot be modified while the job is unsuspended or finished.\n   511→\t//\n   512→\t// +optional\n   513→\tStartTime *metav1.Time\n   514→\n   515→\t// Represents time when the job was completed. It is not guaranteed to\n   516→\t// be set in happens-before order across separate operations.\n   517→\t// It is represented in RFC3339 form and is in UTC.\n   518→\t// The completion time is set when the job finishes successfully, and only then.\n   519→\t// The value cannot be updated or removed. The value indicates the same or\n   520→\t// later point in time as the startTime field.\n   521→\t// +optional\n   522→\tCompletionTime *metav1.Time\n   523→\n   524→\t// The number of pending and running pods which are not terminating (without\n   525→\t// a deletionTimestamp).\n   526→\t// The value is zero for finished jobs.\n   527→\t// +optional\n   528→\tActive int32\n   529→\n   530→\t// The number of pods which are terminating (in phase Pending or Running\n   531→\t// and have a deletionTimestamp).\n   532→\t//\n   533→\t// This field is beta-level. The indexes are represented as decimal integers\n   556→\t// separated by commas. The numbers are listed in increasing order. Three or\n   557→\t// more consecutive numbers are compressed and represented by the first and\n   558→\t// last element of the series, separated by a hyphen.\n   559→\t// For example, if the completed indexes are 1, 3, 4, 5 and 7, they are\n   560→\t// represented as \"1,3-5,7\".\n   561→\t// +optional\n   562→\tCompletedIndexes string\n   563→\n   564→\t// FailedIndexes holds the failed indexes when spec.backoffLimitPerIndex is set.\n   565→\t// The indexes are represented in the text format analogous as for the\n   566→\t// `completedIndexes` field, ie. they are kept as decimal integers\n   567→\t// separated by commas. The numbers are listed in increasing order. Three or\n   568→\t// more consecutive numbers are compressed and represented by the first and\n   569→\t// last element of the series, separated by a hyphen.\n   570→\t// For example, if the failed indexes are 1, 3, 4, 5 and 7, they are\n   571→\t// represented as \"1,3-5,7\".\n   572→\t// The set of failed indexes cannot overlap with the set of completed indexes.\n   573→\t//\n   574→\t// This field is beta-level. Containers completed with success (exit code 0) are\n\t// excluded from the requirement check. Possible values are:\n\t//\n\t// - In: the requirement is satisfied if at least one container exit code\n\t//   (might be multiple if there are multiple containers not restricted\n\t//   by the 'containerName' field) is in the set of specified values.\n\t// - NotIn: the requirement is satisfied if at least one container exit code\n\t//   (might be multiple if there are multiple containers not restricted\n\t//   by the 'containerName' field) is not in the set of specified values.\n\t// Additional values are considered to be added in the future. Clients should\n\t// react to an unknown operator by assuming the requirement is not satisfied.\n\tOperator PodFailurePolicyOnExitCodesOperator\n\n\t// Specifies the set of values. Each returned container exit code (might be\n\t// multiple in case of multiple containers) is checked against this set of\n\t// values with respect to the operator. The list of values must be ordered\n\t// and must not contain duplicates. Value '0' cannot be used for the In operator.\n\t// At least one element is required. At most 255 elements are allowed.\n\t// +listType=set\n\tValues []int32\n}\n\n// PodFailurePolicyOnPodConditionsPattern describes a pattern for matching\n// an actual pod condition type.\ntype PodFailurePolicyOnPodConditionsPattern struct {\n\t// Specifies the required Pod condition type. It can be used when the\n\t//   `JobBackoffLimitPerIndex` feature gate is enabled (disabled by default).\n\t// - Ignore: indicates that the counter towards the .backoffLimit is not\n\t//   incremented and a replacement pod is created.\n\t// - Count: indicates that the pod is handled in the default way - the\n\t//   counter towards the .backoffLimit is incremented.\n\t// Additional values are considered to be added in the future. At most 20 elements are allowed.\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\t// +optional\n\tOnPodConditions []PodFailurePolicyOnPodConditionsPattern\n}\n\n// PodFailurePolicy describes how failed pods influence the backoffLimit.\ntype PodFailurePolicy struct {\n\t// A list of pod failure policy rules. The rules are evaluated in order.\n\t// Once a rule matches a Pod failure, the remaining of the rules are ignored.\n\t// When no rule matches the Pod failure, the default handling applies - the\n\t// counter of pod failures is incremented and it is checked against\n\t// the backoffLimit. At most 20 elements are allowed.\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tRules []PodFailurePolicyRule\n}\n\n// SuccessPolicy describes when a Job can be declared as succeeded based on the success of some indexes.\ntype SuccessPolicy struct {\n\t// rules represents the list of alternative rules for the declaring the Jobs\n\t// as successful before `.status.succeeded >= .spec.completions`. Once any of the rules are met,\n\t// the \"SucceededCriteriaMet\" condition is added, and the lingering pods are removed.\n\t// The terminal state for such a Job has the \"Complete\" condition.\n\t// Additionally, these rules are evaluated in order; Once the Job meets one of the rules,\n\t// other rules are ignored. At most 20 elements are allowed.\n\t// +listType=atomic\n\tRules []SuccessPolicyRule\n}\n\n// SuccessPolicyRule describes rule for declaring a Job as succeeded.\n// Each rule must have at least one of the \"succeededIndexes\" or \"succeededCount\" specified.\ntype SuccessPolicyRule struct {\n\t// succeededIndexes specifies the set of indexes\n\t// which need to be contained in the actual set of the succeeded indexes for the Job.\n\t// The list of indexes must be within 0 to \".spec.completions-1\" and\n\t// must not contain duplicates. At least one element is required.\n\t// The indexes are represented as intervals separated by commas.\n\t// The intervals can be a decimal integer or a pair of decimal integers separated by a hyphen.\n\t// The number are listed in represented by the first and last element of the series,\n\t// separated by a hyphen.\n\t// For example, if the completed indexes are 1, 3, 4, 5 and 7, they are\n\t// represented as \"1,3-5,7\".\n\t// When this field is null, this field doesn't default to any value\n\t// and is never evaluated at any time.\n\t//\n\t// +optional\n\tSucceededIndexes *string\n\n\t// succeededCount specifies the minimal required size of the actual set of the succeeded indexes\n\t// for the Job. When succeededCount is used along with succeededIndexes, the check is\n\t// constrained only to the set of indexes specified by succeededIndexes.\n\t// For example, given that succeededIndexes is \"1-4\", succeededCount is \"3\",\n\t// and completed indexes are \"1\", \"3\", and \"5\", the Job isn't declared as succeeded\n\t// because only \"1\" and \"3\" indexes are considered in that rules.\n\t// When this field is null, this doesn't default to any value and\n\t// is never evaluated at any time.\n\t// When specified it needs to be a positive integer.\n\t//\n\t// +optional\n\tSucceededCount *int32\n}\n\n// JobSpec describes how the job execution will look like.\ntype JobSpec struct {\n\n\t// Specifies the maximum desired number of pods the job should\n\t// run at any given time.
